You might\n964: want to setup a larger cache if you run ASAN builds.\n965: \n966: NOTE: Using docker to run remote cache server described in remote cache docs will likely have\n967: slower cache performance on macOS due to slow disk performance on Docker for Mac.\n968: \n969: Adding the following parameter to Bazel everytime or persist them in `.bazelrc`.\n970: \n971: ```\n972: --remote_cache=http://127.0.0.1:28080/\n973: ```\n974: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/envoy--v1.32.1@b35dd17bea856e19fc4e65fb05e68170841d3726/-/blob/bazel/README.md"}}}

Developers\\n10: may work with the latest build image SHA in [envoy-build-tools](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy-build-tools/blob/main/toolchains/rbe_toolchains_config.bzl#L8)\\n11: repo to provide a self-contained environment for building Envoy binaries and running tests that reflects the latest built Ubuntu Envoy image.\\n12: Moreover, the Docker image at [`envoyproxy/envoy:dev-<hash>`](https://hub.docker.com/r/envoyproxy/envoy/tags?name=dev) is an image that has an Envoy binary at `/usr/local/bin/envoy`.\\n13: The `<hash>` corresponds to the main commit at which the binary was compiled. Lastly, `envoyproxy/envoy:dev` contains an Envoy\\n14: binary built from the latest tip of main that passed tests.\\n15: \\n16: ## Distroless Envoy image\\n17: \\n18: Minimal images based on a [distroless](https://github.com/GoogleContainerTools/distroless) allow for quicker deployment of Envoy.\\n19: \\n20: The Distroless base image is only built with symbols stripped.\\n21: \\n22: ## Debug Envoy image\\n23: \\n24: To get the binary with symbols, use the corresponding Ubuntu based debug image. The image is pushed with two different tags:\\n25: `<hash>` and `latest`. Parallel to the Ubuntu images above, `<hash>` corresponds to the\\n26: main commit at which the binary was compiled, and `latest` corresponds to a binary built from the latest tip of main that passed tests.\\n27: \\n28: ## Windows 2019 Envoy image\\n29: \\n30: On August 31, 2023 the Envoy project ended official Windows support due to a lack of resources.\\n31: We will continue to accept patches related to the Windows build. Until further notice, Windows\\n32: builds are excluded from Envoy CI, as well as the Envoy release and security processes.\\n33: \\n34: The Windows 2019 based Envoy Docker image at [`envoyproxy/envoy-build-windows2019:<hash>`](https://hub.docker.com/r/envoyproxy/envoy-build-windows2019/)\\n35: is used for CI checks, where `<hash>` is specified in [`envoy_build_sha.sh`](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/ci/envoy_build_sha.sh).\\n36: Developers may work with the most recent `envoyproxy/envoy-build-windows2019` image to provide a self-contained environment for building Envoy binaries and\\n37: running tests that reflects the latest built Windows 2019 Envoy image.\\n38: \\n39: # Build image base and compiler versions\\n40: \\n41: Currently there are three build images for Linux and one for Windows:\\n42: \\n43: * `envoyproxy/envoy-build` &mdash; alias to `envoyproxy/envoy-build-ubuntu`.\\n44: * `envoyproxy/envoy-build-ubuntu` &mdash; based on Ubuntu 20.04 (Focal) with GCC 9 and Clang 14 compiler.\\n45: * `envoyproxy/envoy-build-centos` &mdash; based on CentOS 7 with GCC 9 and Clang 14 compiler, this image is experimental and not well tested.\\n46: * `envoyproxy/envoy-build-windows2019` &mdash; based on Windows ltsc2019 with VS 2019 Build Tools, as well as LLVM.\\n47: \\n48: The source for these images is located in the [envoyproxy/envoy-build-tools](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy-build-tools)\\n49: repository.\\n50: \\n51: We use the Clang compiler for all Linux CI runs with tests. We have an additional Linux CI run with GCC which builds binary only.\\n52: \\n53: # C++ standard library\\n54: \\n55: As of November 2019 after [#8859](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/pull/8859) the official released binary is\\n56: [linked against libc++ on Linux](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/bazel/README.md#linking-against-libc-on-linux).\\n57: To override the C++ standard library in your build, set environment variable `ENVOY_STDLIB` to `libstdc++` or `libc++` and\\n58: run `./ci/do_ci.sh` as described below.\\n59: \\n60: # Building and running tests as a developer\\n61: \\n62: The `./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh` script can be used to set up a Docker container on Linux and Windows\\n63: to build an Envoy static binary and run tests.\\n64: \\n65: The build image defaults to `envoyproxy/envoy-build-ubuntu` on Linux and\\n66: `envoyproxy/envoy-build-windows2019` on Windows, but you can choose build image by setting\\n67: `IMAGE_NAME` in the environment.\\n68: \\n69: In case your setup is behind a proxy, set `http_proxy` and `https_proxy` to the proxy servers before\\n70: invoking the build.\\n71: \\n72: ```bash\\n73: IMAGE_NAME=envoyproxy/envoy-build-ubuntu http_proxy=http://proxy.foo.com:8080 https_proxy=http://proxy.bar.com:8080 ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh <build_script_args>\\n74: ```\\n75: \\n76: Besides `http_proxy` and `https_proxy`, maybe you need to set `go_proxy` to replace the default GOPROXY in China.\\n77: \\n78: ```bash\\n79: IMAGE_NAME=envoyproxy/envoy-build-ubuntu go_proxy=https://goproxy.cn,direct http_proxy=http://proxy.foo.com:8080 https_proxy=http://proxy.bar.com:8080 ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh <build_script_args>\\n80: ```\\n81: \\n82: To force the Envoy build image to be refreshed by Docker you can set `ENVOY_DOCKER_PULL=true`.\\n83: \\n84: ```bash\\n85: ENVOY_DOCKER_PULL=true ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh <build_script_args>\\n86: ```\\n87: \\n88: \\n89: # Generating compile commands\\n90: \\n91: The `./ci/do_ci.sh` script provides a CI target that generates compile commands for clangd or other tools.\\n92: \\n93: ```bash\\n94: ENVOY_GEN_COMPDB_OPTIONS=\\\"--vscode --exclude_contrib\\\" ./ci/do_ci.sh refresh_compdb\\n95: ```\\n96: \\n97: ## On Linux\\n98: \\n99: An example basic invocation to build a developer version of the Envoy static binary (using the Bazel `fastbuild` type) is:\\n100: \\n101: ```bash\\n102: ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh dev'\\n103: ```\\n104: \\n105: The Envoy binary can be found in `/tmp/envoy-docker-build/envoy/source/exe/envoy-fastbuild` on the Docker host. You\\n106: can control this by setting `ENVOY_DOCKER_BUILD_DIR` in the environment, e.g. to\\n107: generate the binary in `~/build/envoy/source/exe/envoy-fastbuild` you can run:\\n108: \\n109: ```bash\\n110: ENVOY_DOCKER_BUILD_DIR=~/build ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh dev'\\n111: ```\\n112: \\n113: For a release version of the Envoy binary you can run:\\n114: \\n115: ```bash\\n116: ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh release.server_only'\\n117: ```\\n118: \\n119: The build artifact can be found in `/tmp/envoy-docker-build/envoy/source/exe/envoy` (or wherever\\n120: `$ENVOY_DOCKER_BUILD_DIR` points).\\n121: \\n122: To enable the previous behavior of the `release.server_only` target where the final binary was copied to a tar.gz file\\n123: (e.g. envoy-binary.tar.gz), you can run:\\n124: \\n125:   ```bash\\n126:   ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh release.server_only.binary'\\n127:   ```\\n128: \\n129: For a debug version of the Envoy binary you can run:\\n130: \\n131: ```bash\\n132: ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh debug.server_only'\\n133: ```\\n134: \\n135: The build artifact can be found in `/tmp/envoy-docker-build/envoy/source/exe/envoy-debug` (or wherever\\n136: `$ENVOY_DOCKER_BUILD_DIR` points).\\n137: \\n138: To leverage a [bazel remote cache](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/tree/main/bazel#advanced-caching-setup):\\n139: 1. add bazel options like `--remote_cache` and/or `--remote_cache_header` to a `.bazelrc` file, such as `user.bazelrc`. For example\\n140: \\n141: ```bash\\n142: build:my-remote-cache --remote_cache=grpcs://remotecache.googleapis.com\\n143: build:my-remote-cache --remote_cache_header=Authorization=\\\"Bearer <token>\\\"\\n144: ```\\n145: \\n146: 2. specify the config in the `BAZEL_BUILD_EXTRA_OPTIONS` environment variable. Run\\n147: \\n148: ```bash\\n149: export BAZEL_BUILD_EXTRA_OPTIONS=--config=my-remote-cache\\n150: ```\\n151: \\n152: The `./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh <TARGET>'` targets are:\\n153: \\n154: * `api` &mdash; build and run API tests under `-c fastbuild` with clang.\\n155: * `asan` &mdash; build and run tests under `-c dbg --config=clang-asan` with clang.\\n156: * `asan <test>` &mdash; build and run a specified test or test dir under `-c dbg --config=clang-asan` with clang.\\n157: * `debug` &mdash; build Envoy static binary and run tests under `-c dbg`.\\n158: * `debug <test>` &mdash; build Envoy static binary and run a specified test or test dir under `-c dbg`.\\n159: * `debug.server_only` &mdash; build Envoy static binary under `-c dbg`.\\n160: * `docker` &mdash; build Docker images, expects `release` or `release.server_only` to have been run first.\\n161: * `dev` &mdash; build Envoy static binary and run tests under `-c fastbuild` with clang.\\n162: * `dev <test>` &mdash; build Envoy static binary and run a specified test or test dir under `-c fastbuild` with clang.\\n163: * `dev.contrib` &mdash; build Envoy static binary with contrib and run tests under `-c fastbuild` with clang.\\n164: * `dev.contrib <test>` &mdash; build Envoy static binary with contrib and run a specified test or test dir under `-c fastbuild` with clang.\\n165: * `release` &mdash; build Envoy static binary and run tests under `-c opt` with clang.\\n166: * `release <test>` &mdash; build Envoy static binaries and run a specified test or test dir under `-c opt` with clang.\\n167: * `release.server_only` &mdash; build Envoy static binaries under `-c opt` with clang.\\n168: * `sizeopt` &mdash; build Envoy static binary and run tests under `-c opt --config=sizeopt` with clang.\\n169: * `sizeopt <test>` &mdash; build Envoy static binary and run a specified test or test dir under `-c opt --config=sizeopt` with clang.\\n170: * `sizeopt.server_only` &mdash; build Envoy static binary under `-c opt --config=sizeopt` with clang.\\n171: * `coverage` &mdash; build and run tests under `-c dbg` with gcc, generating coverage information in `$ENVOY_DOCKER_BUILD_DIR/envoy/generated/coverage/coverage.html`.\\n172: * `coverage <test>` &mdash; build and run a specified test or test dir under `-c dbg` with gcc, generating coverage information in `$ENVOY_DOCKER_BUILD_DIR/envoy/generated/coverage/coverage.html`. Specify `//contrib/...` to get contrib coverage.\\n173: * `msan` &mdash; build and run tests under `-c dbg --config=clang-msan` with clang.\\n174: * `msan <test>` &mdash; build and run a specified test or test dir under `-c dbg --config=clang-msan` with clang.\\n175: * `tsan` &mdash; build and run tests under `-c dbg --config=clang-tsan` with clang.\\n176: * `tsan <test>` &mdash; build and run a specified test or test dir under `-c dbg --config=clang-tsan` with clang.\\n177: * `fuzz` &mdash; build and run fuzz tests under `-c dbg --config=asan-fuzzer` with clang.\\n178: * `fuzz <test>` &mdash; build and run a specified fuzz test or test dir under `-c dbg --config=asan-fuzzer` with clang. If specifying a single fuzz test, must use the full target name with \\\"_with_libfuzzer\\\" for `<test>`.\\n179: * `compile_time_options` &mdash; build Envoy and run tests with various compile-time options toggled to their non-default state, to ensure they still build.\\n180: * `compile_time_options <test>` &mdash; build Envoy and run a specified test or test dir with various compile-time options toggled to their non-default state, to ensure they still build.\\n181: * `clang_tidy <files>` &mdash; build and run clang-tidy specified source files, if no files specified, runs against the diff with the last GitHub commit.\\n182: * `check_proto_format`&mdash; check configuration, formatting and build issues in API proto files.\\n183: * `fix_proto_format`&mdash; fix configuration, formatting and build issues in API proto files.\\n184: * `check_and_fix_proto_format` &mdash; check and fix configuration, fomatting and build issues in API proto files.\\n185: * `format`&mdash; run validation, linting and formatting tools.\\n186: * `docs`&mdash; build documentation tree in `generated/docs`.\\n187: \\n188: ## On Windows\\n189: \\n190: An example basic invocation to build the Envoy static binary and run tests is:\\n191: \\n192: ```bash\\n193: ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/windows_ci_steps.sh'\\n194: ```\\n195: \\n196: You can pass additional command line arguments to `./ci/windows_ci_steps.sh` to list specific `bazel` arguments and build/test targets.\\n197: as set environment variables to adjust your container build environment as described above.\\n198: \\n199: The Envoy binary can be found in `${TEMP}\\\\envoy-docker-build\\\\envoy\\\\source\\\\exe` on the Docker host. You\\n200: can control this by setting `ENVOY_DOCKER_BUILD_DIR` in the environment, e.g. to\\n201: generate the binary in `C:\\\\Users\\\\foo\\\\build\\\\envoy\\\\source\\\\exe` you can run:\\n202: \\n203: ```bash\\n204: ENVOY_DOCKER_BUILD_DIR=\\\"C:\\\\Users\\\\foo\\\\build\\\" ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/windows_ci_steps.sh'\\n205: ```\\n206: \\n207: Note the quotations around the `ENVOY_DOCKER_BUILD_DIR` value to preserve the backslashes in the\\n208: path.\\n209: \\n210: If you would like to run an interactive session to keep the build container running (to persist your local build environment), run:\\n211: \\n212: ```bash\\n213: ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh 'bash'\\n214: ```\\n215: \\n216: From an interactive session, you can invoke `bazel` directly, or use the `./ci/windows_ci_steps.sh` script to build and run tests.\\n217: Bazel will look for .bazelrc in the `${HOME}` path, which is mapped to the persistent path `${TEMP}\\\\envoy-docker-build\\\\` on the\\n218: Docker host.\\n219: \\n220: # Testing changes to the build image as a developer\\n221: \\n222: The base build image used in the CI flows here lives in the [envoy-build-tools](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy-build-tools)\\n223: repository. If you need to make and/or test changes to the build image, instructions to do so can be found in\\n224: the [build_container](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy-build-tools/blob/main/build_container/README.md) folder.\\n225: See the Dockerfiles and build scripts there for building a new image.\\n226: \\n227: # macOS Build Flow\\n228: \\n229: The macOS CI build is part of the [Azure Pipelines](https://dev.azure.com/cncf/envoy/_build) workflow.\\n230: Dependencies are installed by the `ci/mac_ci_setup.sh` script, via [Homebrew](https://brew.sh),\\n231: which is pre-installed on the [Azure Pipelines macOS image](https://github.com/actions/virtual-environments/blob/main/images/macos/macos-10.15-Readme.md).\\n232: The dependencies are cached and re-installed on every build. The `ci/mac_ci_steps.sh` script executes the specific commands that\\n233: build and test Envoy. Note that the full version of Xcode (not just Command Line Tools) is required.\\n234: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/envoy--v1.32.1@b35dd17bea856e19fc4e65fb05e68170841d3726/-/blob/ci/README.md\"}"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"5157fe49-4634-41ea-9ff4-b2bcc3cbdc75","uuid":"cda260da-c629-41fd-b566-8af16e81baec","tool_use_result":{"content":"{\"content\":\"1: # Developer use of CI Docker images\\n2: \\n3: There are two available flavors of Envoy Docker images for Linux, based on Ubuntu and Alpine Linux\\n4: and an image based on Windows2019.\\n5: \\n6: ## Ubuntu Envoy image\\n7: \\n8: The Ubuntu based Envoy Docker image at [`envoyproxy/envoy-build-ubuntu:<hash>`](https://hub.docker.com/r/envoyproxy/envoy-build/) is used for CI checks,\\n9: where `<hash>` is specified in [`envoy_build_sha.sh`](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/ci/envoy_build_sha.sh). Developers\\n10: may work with the latest build image SHA in [envoy-build-tools](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy-build-tools/blob/main/toolchains/rbe_toolchains_config.bzl#L8)\\n11: repo to provide a self-contained environment for building Envoy binaries and running tests that reflects the latest built Ubuntu Envoy image.\\n12: Moreover, the Docker image at [`envoyproxy/envoy:dev-<hash>`](https://hub.docker.com/r/envoyproxy/envoy/tags?name=dev) is an image that has an Envoy binary at `/usr/local/bin/envoy`.\\n13: The `<hash>` corresponds to the main commit at which the binary was compiled. Lastly, `envoyproxy/envoy:dev` contains an Envoy\\n14: binary built from the latest tip of main that passed tests.\\n15: \\n16: ## Distroless Envoy image\\n17: \\n18: Minimal images based on a [distroless](https://github.com/GoogleContainerTools/distroless) allow for quicker deployment of Envoy.\\n19: \\n20: The Distroless base image is only built with symbols stripped.\\n21: \\n22: ## Debug Envoy image\\n23: \\n24: To get the binary with symbols, use the corresponding Ubuntu based debug image. The image is pushed with two different tags:\\n25: `<hash>` and `latest`. Parallel to the Ubuntu images above, `<hash>` corresponds to the\\n26: main commit at which the binary was compiled, and `latest` corresponds to a binary built from the latest tip of main that passed tests.\\n27: \\n28: ## Windows 2019 Envoy image\\n29: \\n30: On August 31, 2023 the Envoy project ended official Windows support due to a lack of resources.\\n31: We will continue to accept patches related to the Windows build. Until further notice, Windows\\n32: builds are excluded from Envoy CI, as well as the Envoy release and security processes.\\n33: \\n34: The Windows 2019 based Envoy Docker image at [`envoyproxy/envoy-build-windows2019:<hash>`](https://hub.docker.com/r/envoyproxy/envoy-build-windows2019/)\\n35: is used for CI checks, where `<hash>` is specified in [`envoy_build_sha.sh`](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/ci/envoy_build_sha.sh).\\n36: Developers may work with the most recent `envoyproxy/envoy-build-windows2019` image to provide a self-contained environment for building Envoy binaries and\\n37: running tests that reflects the latest built Windows 2019 Envoy image.\\n38: \\n39: # Build image base and compiler versions\\n40: \\n41: Currently there are three build images for Linux and one for Windows:\\n42: \\n43: * `envoyproxy/envoy-build` &mdash; alias to `envoyproxy/envoy-build-ubuntu`.\\n44: * `envoyproxy/envoy-build-ubuntu` &mdash; based on Ubuntu 20.04 (Focal) with GCC 9 and Clang 14 compiler.\\n45: * `envoyproxy/envoy-build-centos` &mdash; based on CentOS 7 with GCC 9 and Clang 14 compiler, this image is experimental and not well tested.\\n46: * `envoyproxy/envoy-build-windows2019` &mdash; based on Windows ltsc2019 with VS 2019 Build Tools, as well as LLVM.\\n47: \\n48: The source for these images is located in the [envoyproxy/envoy-build-tools](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy-build-tools)\\n49: repository.\\n50: \\n51: We use the Clang compiler for all Linux CI runs with tests. We have an additional Linux CI run with GCC which builds binary only.\\n52: \\n53: # C++ standard library\\n54: \\n55: As of November 2019 after [#8859](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/pull/8859) the official released binary is\\n56: [linked against libc++ on Linux](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/bazel/README.md#linking-against-libc-on-linux).\\n57: To override the C++ standard library in your build, set environment variable `ENVOY_STDLIB` to `libstdc++` or `libc++` and\\n58: run `./ci/do_ci.sh` as described below.\\n59: \\n60: # Building and running tests as a developer\\n61: \\n62: The `./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh` script can be used to set up a Docker container on Linux and Windows\\n63: to build an Envoy static binary and run tests.\\n64: \\n65: The build image defaults to `envoyproxy/envoy-build-ubuntu` on Linux and\\n66: `envoyproxy/envoy-build-windows2019` on Windows, but you can choose build image by setting\\n67: `IMAGE_NAME` in the environment.\\n68: \\n69: In case your setup is behind a proxy, set `http_proxy` and `https_proxy` to the proxy servers before\\n70: invoking the build.\\n71: \\n72: ```bash\\n73: IMAGE_NAME=envoyproxy/envoy-build-ubuntu http_proxy=http://proxy.foo.com:8080 https_proxy=http://proxy.bar.com:8080 ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh <build_script_args>\\n74: ```\\n75: \\n76: Besides `http_proxy` and `https_proxy`, maybe you need to set `go_proxy` to replace the default GOPROXY in China.\\n77: \\n78: ```bash\\n79: IMAGE_NAME=envoyproxy/envoy-build-ubuntu go_proxy=https://goproxy.cn,direct http_proxy=http://proxy.foo.com:8080 https_proxy=http://proxy.bar.com:8080 ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh <build_script_args>\\n80: ```\\n81: \\n82: To force the Envoy build image to be refreshed by Docker you can set `ENVOY_DOCKER_PULL=true`.\\n83: \\n84: ```bash\\n85: ENVOY_DOCKER_PULL=true ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh <build_script_args>\\n86: ```\\n87: \\n88: \\n89: # build and run a specified test or test dir under `-c dbg` with gcc, generating coverage information in `$ENVOY_DOCKER_BUILD_DIR/envoy/generated/coverage/coverage.html`. Specify `//contrib/...` to get contrib coverage.\\n173: * `msan` &mdash; build and run tests under `-c dbg --config=clang-msan` with clang.\\n174: * `msan <test>` &mdash; build and run a specified test or test dir under `-c dbg --config=clang-msan` with clang.\\n175: * `tsan` &mdash; build and run tests under `-c dbg --config=clang-tsan` with clang.\\n176: * `tsan <test>` &mdash; build and run a specified test or test dir under `-c dbg --config=clang-tsan` with clang.\\n177: * `fuzz` &mdash; build and run fuzz tests under `-c dbg --config=asan-fuzzer` with clang.\\n178: * `fuzz <test>` &mdash; build and run a specified fuzz test or test dir under `-c dbg --config=asan-fuzzer` with clang. If specifying a single fuzz test, must use the full target name with \\\"_with_libfuzzer\\\" for `<test>`.\\n179: * `compile_time_options` &mdash; build Envoy and run tests with various compile-time options toggled to their non-default state, to ensure they still build.\\n180: * `compile_time_options <test>` &mdash; build Envoy and run a specified test or test dir with various compile-time options toggled to their non-default state, to ensure they still build.\\n181: * `clang_tidy <files>` &mdash; build and run clang-tidy specified source files, if no files specified, runs against the diff with the last GitHub commit.\\n182: * `check_proto_format`&mdash; check configuration, formatting and build issues in API proto files.\\n183: * `fix_proto_format`&mdash; fix configuration, formatting and build issues in API proto files.\\n184: * `check_and_fix_proto_format` &mdash; check and fix configuration, fomatting and build issues in API proto files.\\n185: * `format`&mdash; run validation, linting and formatting tools.\\n186: * `docs`&mdash; build documentation tree in `generated/docs`.\\n187: \\n188: ## On Windows\\n189: \\n190: An example basic invocation to build the Envoy static binary and run tests is:\\n191: \\n192: ```bash\\n193: ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/windows_ci_steps.sh'\\n194: ```\\n195: \\n196: You can pass additional command line arguments to `./ci/windows_ci_steps.sh` to list specific `bazel` arguments and build/test targets.\\n197: as set environment variables to adjust your container build environment as described above.\\n198: \\n199: The Envoy binary can be found in `${TEMP}\\\\envoy-docker-build\\\\envoy\\\\source\\\\exe` on the Docker host. You\\n200: can control this by setting `ENVOY_DOCKER_BUILD_DIR` in the environment, e.g. to\\n201: generate the binary in `C:\\\\Users\\\\foo\\\\build\\\\envoy\\\\source\\\\exe` you can run:\\n202: \\n203: ```bash\\n204: ENVOY_DOCKER_BUILD_DIR=\\\"C:\\\\Users\\\\foo\\\\build\\\" ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/windows_ci_steps.sh'\\n205: ```\\n206: \\n207: Note the quotations around the `ENVOY_DOCKER_BUILD_DIR` value to preserve the backslashes in the\\n208: path.\\n209: \\n210: If you would like to run an interactive session to keep the build container running (to persist your local build environment), run:\\n211: \\n212: ```bash\\n213: ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh 'bash'\\n214: ```\\n215: \\n216: From an interactive session, you can invoke `bazel` directly, or use the `./ci/windows_ci_steps.sh` script to build and run tests.\\n217: Bazel will look for .bazelrc in the `${HOME}` path, which is mapped to the persistent path `${TEMP}\\\\envoy-docker-build\\\\` on the\\n218: Docker host.\\n219: \\n220: # Testing changes to the build image as a developer\\n221: \\n222: The base build image used in the CI flows here lives in the [envoy-build-tools](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy-build-tools)\\n223: repository. If you need to make and/or test changes to the build image, instructions to do so can be found in\\n224: the [build_container](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy-build-tools/blob/main/build_container/README.md) folder.\\n225: See the Dockerfiles and build scripts there for building a new image.\\n226: \\n227: # macOS Build Flow\\n228: \\n229: The macOS CI build is part of the [Azure Pipelines](https://dev.azure.com/cncf/envoy/_build) workflow.\\n230: Dependencies are installed by the `ci/mac_ci_setup.sh` script, via [Homebrew](https://brew.sh),\\n231: which is pre-installed on the [Azure Pipelines macOS image](https://github.com/actions/virtual-environments/blob/main/images/macos/macos-10.15-Readme.md).\\n232: The dependencies are cached and re-installed on every build. The `ci/mac_ci_steps.sh` script executes the specific commands that\\n233: build and test Envoy. Note that the full version of Xcode (not just Command Line Tools) is required.\\n234: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/envoy--v1.32.1@b35dd17bea856e19fc4e65fb05e68170841d3726/-/blob/ci/README.md\"}","structuredContent":{"content":"1: # Developer use of CI Docker images\n2: \n3: There are two available flavors of Envoy Docker images for Linux, based on Ubuntu and Alpine Linux\n4: and an image based on Windows2019.\n5: \n6: ## Ubuntu Envoy image\n7: \n8: The Ubuntu based Envoy Docker image at [`envoyproxy/envoy-build-ubuntu:<hash>`](https://hub.docker.com/r/envoyproxy/envoy-build/) is used for CI checks,\n9: where `<hash>` is specified in [`envoy_build_sha.sh`](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/ci/envoy_build_sha.sh). Developers\n10: may work with the latest build image SHA in [envoy-build-tools](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy-build-tools/blob/main/toolchains/rbe_toolchains_config.bzl#L8)\n11: repo to provide a self-contained environment for building Envoy binaries and running tests that reflects the latest built Ubuntu Envoy image.\n12: Moreover, the Docker image at [`envoyproxy/envoy:dev-<hash>`](https://hub.docker.com/r/envoyproxy/envoy/tags?name=dev) is an image that has an Envoy binary at `/usr/local/bin/envoy`.\n13: The `<hash>` corresponds to the main commit at which the binary was compiled. Lastly, `envoyproxy/envoy:dev` contains an Envoy\n14: binary built from the latest tip of main that passed tests.\n15: \n16: ## Distroless Envoy image\n17: \n18: Minimal images based on a [distroless](https://github.com/GoogleContainerTools/distroless) allow for quicker deployment of Envoy.\n19: \n20: The Distroless base image is only built with symbols stripped.\n21: \n22: ## Debug Envoy image\n23: \n24: To get the binary with symbols, use the corresponding Ubuntu based debug image. The image is pushed with two different tags:\n25: `<hash>` and `latest`. Parallel to the Ubuntu images above, `<hash>` corresponds to the\n26: main commit at which the binary was compiled, and `latest` corresponds to a binary built from the latest tip of main that passed tests.\n27: \n28: ## Windows 2019 Envoy image\n29: \n30: On August 31, 2023 the Envoy project ended official Windows support due to a lack of resources.\n31: We will continue to accept patches related to the Windows build. Until further notice, Windows\n32: builds are excluded from Envoy CI, as well as the Envoy release and security processes.\n33: \n34: The Windows 2019 based Envoy Docker image at [`envoyproxy/envoy-build-windows2019:<hash>`](https://hub.docker.com/r/envoyproxy/envoy-build-windows2019/)\n35: is used for CI checks, where `<hash>` is specified in [`envoy_build_sha.sh`](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/ci/envoy_build_sha.sh).\n36: Developers may work with the most recent `envoyproxy/envoy-build-windows2019` image to provide a self-contained environment for building Envoy binaries and\n37: running tests that reflects the latest built Windows 2019 Envoy image.\n38: \n39: # Build image base and compiler versions\n40: \n41: Currently there are three build images for Linux and one for Windows:\n42: \n43: * `envoyproxy/envoy-build` &mdash; alias to `envoyproxy/envoy-build-ubuntu`.\n44: * `envoyproxy/envoy-build-ubuntu` &mdash; based on Ubuntu 20.04 (Focal) with GCC 9 and Clang 14 compiler.\n45: * `envoyproxy/envoy-build-centos` &mdash; based on CentOS 7 with GCC 9 and Clang 14 compiler, this image is experimental and not well tested.\n46: * `envoyproxy/envoy-build-windows2019` &mdash; based on Windows ltsc2019 with VS 2019 Build Tools, as well as LLVM.\n47: \n48: The source for these images is located in the [envoyproxy/envoy-build-tools](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy-build-tools)\n49: repository.\n50: \n51: We use the Clang compiler for all Linux CI runs with tests. We have an additional Linux CI run with GCC which builds binary only.\n52: \n53: # C++ standard library\n54: \n55: As of November 2019 after [#8859](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/pull/8859) the official released binary is\n56: [linked against libc++ on Linux](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/bazel/README.md#linking-against-libc-on-linux).\n57: To override the C++ standard library in your build, set environment variable `ENVOY_STDLIB` to `libstdc++` or `libc++` and\n58: run `./ci/do_ci.sh` as described below.\n59: \n60: # Building and running tests as a developer\n61: \n62: The `./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh` script can be used to set up a Docker container on Linux and Windows\n63: to build an Envoy static binary and run tests.\n64: \n65: The build image defaults to `envoyproxy/envoy-build-ubuntu` on Linux and\n66: `envoyproxy/envoy-build-windows2019` on Windows, but you can choose build image by setting\n67: `IMAGE_NAME` in the environment.\n68: \n69: In case your setup is behind a proxy, set `http_proxy` and `https_proxy` to the proxy servers before\n70: invoking the build.\n71: \n72: ```bash\n73: IMAGE_NAME=envoyproxy/envoy-build-ubuntu http_proxy=http://proxy.foo.com:8080 https_proxy=http://proxy.bar.com:8080 ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh <build_script_args>\n74: ```\n75: \n76: Besides `http_proxy` and `https_proxy`, maybe you need to set `go_proxy` to replace the default GOPROXY in China.\n77: \n78: ```bash\n79: IMAGE_NAME=envoyproxy/envoy-build-ubuntu go_proxy=https://goproxy.cn,direct http_proxy=http://proxy.foo.com:8080 https_proxy=http://proxy.bar.com:8080 ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh <build_script_args>\n80: ```\n81: \n82: To force the Envoy build image to be refreshed by Docker you can set `ENVOY_DOCKER_PULL=true`.\n83: \n84: ```bash\n85: ENVOY_DOCKER_PULL=true ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh <build_script_args>\n86: ```\n87: \n88: \n89: # Generating compile commands\n90: \n91: The `./ci/do_ci.sh` script provides a CI target that generates compile commands for clangd or other tools.\n92: \n93: ```bash\n94: ENVOY_GEN_COMPDB_OPTIONS=\"--vscode --exclude_contrib\" ./ci/do_ci.sh refresh_compdb\n95: ```\n96: \n97: ## On Linux\n98: \n99: An example basic invocation to build a developer version of the Envoy static binary (using the Bazel `fastbuild` type) is:\n100: \n101: ```bash\n102: ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh dev'\n103: ```\n104: \n105: The Envoy binary can be found in `/tmp/envoy-docker-build/envoy/source/exe/envoy-fastbuild` on the Docker host. You\n106: can control this by setting `ENVOY_DOCKER_BUILD_DIR` in the environment, e.g. to\n107: generate the binary in `~/build/envoy/source/exe/envoy-fastbuild` you can run:\n108: \n109: ```bash\n110: ENVOY_DOCKER_BUILD_DIR=~/build ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh dev'\n111: ```\n112: \n113: For a release version of the Envoy binary you can run:\n114: \n115: ```bash\n116: ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh release.server_only'\n117: ```\n118: \n119: The build artifact can be found in `/tmp/envoy-docker-build/envoy/source/exe/envoy` (or wherever\n120: `$ENVOY_DOCKER_BUILD_DIR` points).\n121: \n122: To enable the previous behavior of the `release.server_only` target where the final binary was copied to a tar.gz file\n123: (e.g. envoy-binary.tar.gz), you can run:\n124: \n125:   ```bash\n126:   ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh release.server_only.binary'\n127:   ```\n128: \n129: For a debug version of the Envoy binary you can run:\n130: \n131: ```bash\n132: ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh debug.server_only'\n133: ```\n134: \n135: The build artifact can be found in `/tmp/envoy-docker-build/envoy/source/exe/envoy-debug` (or wherever\n136: `$ENVOY_DOCKER_BUILD_DIR` points).\n137: \n138: To leverage a [bazel remote cache](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/tree/main/bazel#advanced-caching-setup):\n139: 1. add bazel options like `--remote_cache` and/or `--remote_cache_header` to a `.bazelrc` file, such as `user.bazelrc`. For example\n140: \n141: ```bash\n142: build:my-remote-cache --remote_cache=grpcs://remotecache.googleapis.com\n143: build:my-remote-cache --remote_cache_header=Authorization=\"Bearer <token>\"\n144: ```\n145: \n146: 2. specify the config in the `BAZEL_BUILD_EXTRA_OPTIONS` environment variable. Run\n147: \n148: ```bash\n149: export BAZEL_BUILD_EXTRA_OPTIONS=--config=my-remote-cache\n150: ```\n151: \n152: The `./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh <TARGET>'` targets are:\n153: \n154: * `api` &mdash; build and run API tests under `-c fastbuild` with clang.\n155: * `asan` &mdash; build and run tests under `-c dbg --config=clang-asan` with clang.\n156: * `asan <test>` &mdash; build and run a specified test or test dir under `-c dbg --config=clang-asan` with clang.\n157: * `debug` &mdash; build Envoy static binary and run tests under `-c dbg`.\n158: * `debug <test>` &mdash; build Envoy static binary and run a specified test or test dir under `-c dbg`.\n159: * `debug.server_only` &mdash; build Envoy static binary under `-c dbg`.\n160: * `docker` &mdash; build Docker images, expects `release` or `release.server_only` to have been run first.\n161: * `dev` &mdash; build Envoy static binary and run tests under `-c fastbuild` with clang.\n162: * `dev <test>` &mdash; build Envoy static binary and run a specified test or test dir under `-c fastbuild` with clang.\n163: * `dev.contrib` &mdash; build Envoy static binary with contrib and run tests under `-c fastbuild` with clang.\n164: * `dev.contrib <test>` &mdash; build Envoy static binary with contrib and run a specified test or test dir under `-c fastbuild` with clang.\n165: * `release` &mdash; build Envoy static binary and run tests under `-c opt` with clang.\n166: * `release <test>` &mdash; build Envoy static binaries and run a specified test or test dir under `-c opt` with clang.\n167: * `release.server_only` &mdash; build Envoy static binaries under `-c opt` with clang.\n168: * `sizeopt` &mdash; build Envoy static binary and run tests under `-c opt --config=sizeopt` with clang.\n169: * `sizeopt <test>` &mdash; build Envoy static binary and run a specified test or test dir under `-c opt --config=sizeopt` with clang.\n170: * `sizeopt.server_only` &mdash; build Envoy static binary under `-c opt --config=sizeopt` with clang.\n171: * `coverage` &mdash; build and run tests under `-c dbg` with gcc, generating coverage information in `$ENVOY_DOCKER_BUILD_DIR/envoy/generated/coverage/coverage.html`.\n172: * `coverage <test>` &mdash; build and run a specified test or test dir under `-c dbg` with gcc, generating coverage information in `$ENVOY_DOCKER_BUILD_DIR/envoy/generated/coverage/coverage.html`. Specify `//contrib/...` to get contrib coverage.\n173: * `msan` &mdash; build and run tests under `-c dbg --config=clang-msan` with clang.\n174: * `msan <test>` &mdash; build and run a specified test or test dir under `-c dbg --config=clang-msan` with clang.\n175: * `tsan` &mdash; build and run tests under `-c dbg --config=clang-tsan` with clang.\n176: * `tsan <test>` &mdash; build and run a specified test or test dir under `-c dbg --config=clang-tsan` with clang.\n177: * `fuzz` &mdash; build and run fuzz tests under `-c dbg --config=asan-fuzzer` with clang.\n178: * `fuzz <test>` &mdash; build and run a specified fuzz test or test dir under `-c dbg --config=asan-fuzzer` with clang. If specifying a single fuzz test, must use the full target name with \"_with_libfuzzer\" for `<test>`.\n179: * `compile_time_options` &mdash; build Envoy and run tests with various compile-time options toggled to their non-default state, to ensure they still build.\n180: * `compile_time_options <test>` &mdash; build Envoy and run a specified test or test dir with various compile-time options toggled to their non-default state, to ensure they still build.\n181: * `clang_tidy <files>` &mdash; build and run clang-tidy specified source files, if no files specified, runs against the diff with the last GitHub commit.\n182: * `check_proto_format`&mdash; check configuration, formatting and build issues in API proto files.\n183: * `fix_proto_format`&mdash; fix configuration, formatting and build issues in API proto files.\n184: * `check_and_fix_proto_format` &mdash; check and fix configuration, fomatting and build issues in API proto files.\n185: * `format`&mdash; run validation, linting and formatting tools.\n186: * `docs`&mdash; build documentation tree in `generated/docs`.\n187: \n188: ## On Windows\n189: \n190: An example basic invocation to build the Envoy static binary and run tests is:\n191: \n192: ```bash\n193: ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/windows_ci_steps.sh'\n194: ```\n195: \n196: You can pass additional command line arguments to `./ci/windows_ci_steps.sh` to list specific `bazel` arguments and build/test targets.\n197: as set environment variables to adjust your container build environment as described above.\n198: \n199: The Envoy binary can be found in `${TEMP}\\envoy-docker-build\\envoy\\source\\exe` on the Docker host. You\n200: can control this by setting `ENVOY_DOCKER_BUILD_DIR` in the environment, e.g. to\n201: generate the binary in `C:\\Users\\foo\\build\\envoy\\source\\exe` you can run:\n202: \n203: ```bash\n204: ENVOY_DOCKER_BUILD_DIR=\"C:\\Users\\foo\\build\" ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/windows_ci_steps.sh'\n205: ```\n206: \n207: Note the quotations around the `ENVOY_DOCKER_BUILD_DIR` value to preserve the backslashes in the\n208: path.\n209: \n210: If you would like to run an interactive session to keep the build container running (to persist your local build environment), run:\n211: \n212: ```bash\n213: ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh 'bash'\n214: ```\n215: \n216: From an interactive session, you can invoke `bazel` directly, or use the `./ci/windows_ci_steps.sh` script to build and run tests.\n217: Bazel will look for .bazelrc in the `${HOME}` path, which is mapped to the persistent path `${TEMP}\\envoy-docker-build\\` on the\n218: Docker host.\n219: \n220: # Testing changes to the build image as a developer\n221: \n222: The base build image used in the CI flows here lives in the [envoy-build-tools](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy-build-tools)\n223: repository. If you need to make and/or test changes to the build image, instructions to do so can be found in\n224: the [build_container](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy-build-tools/blob/main/build_container/README.md) folder.\n225: See the Dockerfiles and build scripts there for building a new image.\n226: \n227: # macOS Build Flow\n228: \n229: The macOS CI build is part of the [Azure Pipelines](https://dev.azure.com/cncf/envoy/_build) workflow.\n230: Dependencies are installed by the `ci/mac_ci_setup.sh` script, via [Homebrew](https://brew.sh),\n231: which is pre-installed on the [Azure Pipelines macOS image](https://github.com/actions/virtual-environments/blob/main/images/macos/macos-10.15-Readme.md).\n232: The dependencies are cached and re-installed on every build. The `ci/mac_ci_steps.sh` script executes the specific commands that\n233: build and test Envoy. {"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01UZpNsbfYi8cKEandpaF8kz","type":"tool_result","content":"{\"content\":\"1: # Repository layout overview\\n2: \\n3: This is a high level overview of how the repository is laid out to both aid in code investigation,\\n4: as well as to clearly specify how extensions are added to the repository. The top level directories\\n5: are:\\n6: \\n7: * [.azure-pipelines/](.azure-pipelines/): Configuration for\\n8: [Azure Pipelines](https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/services/devops/pipelines/).\\n9: * [api/](api/): Envoy data plane API.\\n10: * [bazel/](bazel/): Configuration for Envoy's use of [Bazel](https://bazel.build/).\\n11: * [ci/](ci/): Scripts used both during CI as well as to build Docker containers.\\n12: * [configs/](configs/): Example Envoy configurations.\\n13: * [docs/](docs/): End user facing Envoy proxy and data plane API documentation as well as scripts\\n14:   for publishing final docs during releases.\\n15: * [examples/](examples/): Larger Envoy examples using Docker and Docker Compose.\\n16: * [envoy/](envoy/): \\\"Public\\\" interface headers for \\\"core\\\" Envoy. In general,\\n17:   these are almost entirely 100% abstract classes. There are a few cases of not-abstract classes in\\n18:   the \\\"public\\\" headers, typically for performance reasons. Note that \\\"core\\\" includes some\\n19:   \\\"extensions\\\" such as the HTTP connection manager filter and associated functionality which are\\n20:   so fundamental to Envoy that they will likely never be optional from a compilation perspective.\\n21: * [restarter/](restarter/): Envoy's hot restart wrapper Python script.\\n22: * [security/](security/): Some templates for reporting security issues of Envoy. Historical security issues can also be found here.\\n23: * [source/](source/): Source code for core Envoy as well as extensions. The layout of this directory\\n24:   is discussed in further detail below.\\n25: * [support/](support/): Development support scripts (pre-commit Git hooks, etc.)\\n26: * [test/](test/): Test code for core Envoy as well as extensions. The layout of this directory is\\n27:   discussed in further detail below.\\n28: * [tools/](tools/): Miscellaneous tools that have not found a home somewhere else.\\n29: \\n30: ## [source/](source/)\\n31: \\n32: * [common/](source/common/): Core Envoy code (not specific to extensions) that is also not\\n33:   specific to a standalone server implementation. I.e., this is the code that could be used if Envoy\\n34:   were eventually embedded as a library.\\n35: * [docs/](source/docs/): Miscellaneous developer/design documentation that is not relevant for\\n36:   the public user documentation.\\n37: * [exe/](source/exe/): Code specific to building the final production Envoy server binary. This is\\n38:   the only code that is not shared by integration and unit tests.\\n39: * [extensions/](source/extensions/): Extensions to the core Envoy code. The layout of this\\n40:   directory is discussed in further detail below.\\n41: * [server/](source/server/): Code specific to running Envoy as a standalone server. E.g,\\n42:   configuration, server startup, workers, etc. Over time, the line between `common/` and `server/`\\n43:   has become somewhat blurred. Use best judgment as to where to place something.\\n44: \\n45: ## [test/](test/)\\n46: \\n47: Not every directory within test is described below, but a few highlights:\\n48: \\n49: * Unit tests are found in directories matching their [source/](source/) equivalents. E.g.,\\n50:   [common/](test/common/), [exe/](test/exe/), and [server/](test/server/).\\n51: * Extension unit tests also match their source equivalents in [extensions/](test/extensions/).\\n52: * [integration/](test/integration/) holds end-to-end integration tests using roughly the real\\n53:   Envoy server code, fake downstream clients, and fake upstream servers. Integration tests also\\n54:   test some of the extensions found in the repository. Note that in the future, we would like to\\n55:   allow integration tests that are specific to extensions and are not required for covering\\n56:   \\\"core\\\" Envoy functionality. Those integration tests will likely end up in the\\n57:   [extensions/](test/extensions/) directory but further work and thinking is required before\\n58:   we get to that point.\\n59: * [mocks/](test/mocks/) contains mock implementations of all of the core Envoy interfaces found in\\n60:   [include/](include/).\\n61: * Other directories include tooling used for configuration testing, coverage testing, fuzz testing,\\n62:   common test code, etc.\\n63: \\n64: ## [source/extensions](source/extensions/) layout\\n65: \\n66: We maintain a very specific code and namespace layout for extensions. {"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01GnyFocSwXCh3LKD2R8B3eX","type":"tool_result","content":"{\"content\":\"1: # Envoy tests\\n2: \\n3: Envoy uses the [Google Test framework](https://github.com/google/googletest) for\\n4: tests, including\\n5: [Google Mock](https://github.com/google/googletest/blob/master/googlemock/README.md) for\\n6: mocks and matchers. See the documentation on those pages for information on the\\n7: various classes, macros, and matchers that Envoy uses from those frameworks.\\n8: \\n9: ## Integration tests\\n10: \\n11: Envoy contains an integration testing framework, for testing\\n12: downstream-Envoy-upstream communication.\\n13: [See the framework's README for more information.](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/test/integration/README.md)\\n14: \\n15: ## Custom matchers\\n16: \\n17: Envoy includes some custom Google Mock matchers to make test expectation\\n18: statements simpler to write and easier to understand.\\n19: \\n20: ### HeaderValueOf\\n21: \\n22: Tests that a HeaderMap argument contains exactly one header with the given key,\\n23: whose value satisfies the given expectation. The expectation can be a matcher,\\n24: or a string that the value should equal.\\n25: \\n26: Examples:\\n27: \\n28: ```cpp\\n29: EXPECT_THAT(response->headers(), HeaderValueOf(Headers::get().Server, \\\"envoy\\\"));\\n30: ```\\n31: \\n32: ```cpp\\n33: using testing::HasSubstr;\\n34: EXPECT_THAT(request->headers(),\\n35:             HeaderValueOf(Headers::get().AcceptEncoding, HasSubstr(\\\"gzip\\\")));\\n36: ```\\n37: \\n38: ### HttpStatusIs\\n39: \\n40: Tests that a HeaderMap argument has the provided HTTP status code. The status\\n41: code can be passed in as a string or an integer.\\n42: \\n43: Example:\\n44: \\n45: ```cpp\\n46: EXPECT_THAT(response->headers(), HttpStatusIs(\\\"200\\\"));\\n47: ```\\n48: \\n49: ### HeaderMapEqual and HeaderMapEqualRef\\n50: \\n51: `HeaderMapEqualRef` tests that two `HeaderMap` arguments are equal.\\n52: `HeaderMapEqual` is the same, but it compares two pointers to `HeaderMap`s, and\\n53: the matcher's argument must be a `HeaderMapPtr`.\\n54: \\n55: Example:\\n56: \\n57: ```cpp\\n58: EXPECT_THAT(response->headers(), HeaderMapEqualRef(expected_headers));\\n59: ```\\n60: \\n61: ### ProtoEq, ProtoEqIgnoringField, RepeatedProtoEq\\n62: \\n63: Tests equality of protobufs, with a variant that ignores the value (including\\n64: presence) of a single named field. Another variant can be used to compare two\\n65: instances of Protobuf::RepeatedPtrField element-by-element.\\n66: \\n67: Example:\\n68: \\n69: ```cpp\\n70: envoy::service::discovery::v3::DeltaDiscoveryRequest expected_request;\\n71: // (not shown: set some fields of expected_request...)\\n72: EXPECT_CALL(async_stream_, sendMessage(ProtoEqIgnoringField(expected_request, \\\"response_nonce\\\"), false));\\n73: \\n74: response->mutable_resources()->Add();\\n75: response->mutable_resources()->Add();\\n76: response->mutable_resources()->Add();\\n77: // (not shown: do something to populate those empty added items...)\\n78: EXPECT_CALL(callbacks_, onConfigUpdate(RepeatedProtoEq(response->resources()), version));\\n79: ```\\n80: \\n81: ### IsSubsetOfHeaders and IsSupersetOfHeaders\\n82: \\n83: Tests that one `HeaderMap` argument contains every header in another\\n84: `HeaderMap`.\\n85: \\n86: Examples:\\n87: \\n88: ```cpp\\n89: EXPECT_THAT(response->headers(), IsSubsetOfHeaders(allowed_headers));\\n90: EXPECT_THAT(response->headers(), IsSupersetOfHeaders(required_headers));\\n91: ```\\n92: \\n93: ## Controlling time in tests\\n94: \\n95: In Envoy production code, time and timers are managed via\\n96: [`Event::TimeSystem`](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/include/envoy/event/timer.h),\\n97: which provides a mechanism for querying the time and setting up time-based\\n98: callbacks. Bypassing this abstraction in Envoy code is flagged as a format\\n99: violation in CI.\\n100: \\n101: In tests we use a derivation\\n102: [`Event::TestTimeSystem`](test_common/test_time_system.h) which adds the ability\\n103: to sleep or do a blocking timed wait on a condition variable. There are two\\n104: implementations of the `Event::TestTimeSystem` interface:\\n105: `Event::TestRealTimeSystem`, and `Event::SimulatedTimeSystem`. The latter is\\n106: recommended for all new tests, as it helps avoid flaky tests on slow machines,\\n107: and makes tests run faster.\\n108: \\n109: Typically we do not want to have both real-time and simulated-time in the same\\n110: test; that could lead to hard-to-reproduce results. Thus both implementations\\n111: have a mechanism to enforce that only one of them can be instantiated at once.\\n112: A runtime assertion occurs if an `Event::TestRealTimeSystem` and\\n113: `Event::SimulatedTimeSystem` are instantiated at the same time. Once the\\n114: time-system goes out of scope, usually at the end of a test method, the slate\\n115: is clean and a new test-method can use a different time system.\\n116: \\n117: There is also `Event::GlobalTimeSystem`, which can be instantiated in shared\\n118: test infrastructure that wants to be agnostic to which `TimeSystem` is used in a\\n119: test. When no `TimeSystem` is instantiated in a test, the `Event::GlobalTimeSystem`\\n120: will lazy-initialize itself into a concrete `TimeSystem`. Currently this is\\n121: `TestRealTimeSystem` but will be changed in the future to `SimulatedTimeSystem`.\\n122: \\n123: \\n124: ## Benchmark tests\\n125: \\n126: Envoy uses [Google Benchmark](https://github.com/google/benchmark/) for\\n127: microbenchmarks. There are custom bazel rules, `envoy_cc_benchmark_binary` and\\n128: `envoy_benchmark_test`, to execute them locally and in CI environments\\n129: respectively. `envoy_benchmark_test` rules call the benchmark binary from a\\n130: [script](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/bazel/test_for_benchmark_wrapper.sh)\\n131: which runs the benchmark with a minimal number of iterations and skipping\\n132: expensive benchmarks to quickly verify that the binary is able to run to\\n133: completion. In order to collect meaningful bechmarks, `bazel run -c opt` the\\n134: benchmark binary target on a quiescent machine.\\n135: \\n136: If you would like to detect when your benchmark test is running under the\\n137: wrapper, call\\n138: [`Envoy::benchmark::skipExpensiveBechmarks()`](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/test/benchmark/main.h).\\n139: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/envoy--v1.32.1@b35dd17bea856e19fc4e65fb05e68170841d3726/-/blob/test/README.md\"}"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"5157fe49-4634-41ea-9ff4-b2bcc3cbdc75","uuid":"fb5cd453-1a6a-4df9-a9a7-0f29cd25f3f8","tool_use_result":{"content":"{\"content\":\"1: # Envoy tests\\n2: \\n3: Envoy uses the [Google Test framework](https://github.com/google/googletest) for\\n4: tests, including\\n5: [Google Mock](https://github.com/google/googletest/blob/master/googlemock/README.md) for\\n6: mocks and matchers. The status\n41: code can be passed in as a string or an integer.\n42: \n43: Example:\n44: \n45: ```cpp\n46: EXPECT_THAT(response->headers(), HttpStatusIs(\"200\"));\n47: ```\n48: \n49: ### HeaderMapEqual and HeaderMapEqualRef\n50: \n51: `HeaderMapEqualRef` tests that two `HeaderMap` arguments are equal.\n52: `HeaderMapEqual` is the same, but it compares two pointers to `HeaderMap`s, and\n53: the matcher's argument must be a `HeaderMapPtr`.\n54: \n55: Example:\n56: \n57: ```cpp\n58: EXPECT_THAT(response->headers(), HeaderMapEqualRef(expected_headers));\n59: ```\n60: \n61: ### ProtoEq, ProtoEqIgnoringField, RepeatedProtoEq\n62: \n63: Tests equality of protobufs, with a variant that ignores the value (including\n64: presence) of a single named field. Another variant can be used to compare two\n65: instances of Protobuf::RepeatedPtrField element-by-element.\n66: \n67: Example:\n68: \n69: ```cpp\n70: envoy::service::discovery::v3::DeltaDiscoveryRequest expected_request;\n71: // (not shown: set some fields of expected_request...)\n72: EXPECT_CALL(async_stream_, sendMessage(ProtoEqIgnoringField(expected_request, \"response_nonce\"), false));\n73: \n74: response->mutable_resources()->Add();\n75: response->mutable_resources()->Add();\n76: response->mutable_resources()->Add();\n77: // (not shown: do something to populate those empty added items...)\n78: EXPECT_CALL(callbacks_, onConfigUpdate(RepeatedProtoEq(response->resources()), version));\n79: ```\n80: \n81: ### IsSubsetOfHeaders and IsSupersetOfHeaders\n82: \n83: Tests that one `HeaderMap` argument contains every header in another\n84: `HeaderMap`.\n85: \n86: Examples:\n87: \n88: ```cpp\n89: EXPECT_THAT(response->headers(), IsSubsetOfHeaders(allowed_headers));\n90: EXPECT_THAT(response->headers(), IsSupersetOfHeaders(required_headers));\n91: ```\n92: \n93: ## Controlling time in tests\n94: \n95: In Envoy production code, time and timers are managed via\n96: [`Event::TimeSystem`](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/include/envoy/event/timer.h),\n97: which provides a mechanism for querying the time and setting up time-based\n98: callbacks. Bypassing this abstraction in Envoy code is flagged as a format\n99: violation in CI.\n100: \n101: In tests we use a derivation\n102: [`Event::TestTimeSystem`](test_common/test_time_system.h) which adds the ability\n103: to sleep or do a blocking timed wait on a condition variable. There are two\n104: implementations of the `Event::TestTimeSystem` interface:\n105: `Event::TestRealTimeSystem`, and `Event::SimulatedTimeSystem`. The latter is\n106: recommended for all new tests, as it helps avoid flaky tests on slow machines,\n107: and makes tests run faster.\n108: \n109: Typically we do not want to have both real-time and simulated-time in the same\n110: test; that could lead to hard-to-reproduce results. Thus both implementations\n111: have a mechanism to enforce that only one of them can be instantiated at once.\n112: A runtime assertion occurs if an `Event::TestRealTimeSystem` and\n113: `Event::SimulatedTimeSystem` are instantiated at the same time. Once the\n114: time-system goes out of scope, usually at the end of a test method, the slate\n115: is clean and a new test-method can use a different time system.\n116: \n117: There is also `Event::GlobalTimeSystem`, which can be instantiated in shared\n118: test infrastructure that wants to be agnostic to which `TimeSystem` is used in a\n119: test. When no `TimeSystem` is instantiated in a test, the `Event::GlobalTimeSystem`\n120: will lazy-initialize itself into a concrete `TimeSystem`. Currently this is\n121: `TestRealTimeSystem` but will be changed in the future to `SimulatedTimeSystem`.\n122: \n123: \n124: ## Benchmark tests\n125: \n126: Envoy uses [Google Benchmark](https://github.com/google/benchmark/) for\n127: microbenchmarks. There are custom bazel rules, `envoy_cc_benchmark_binary` and\n128: `envoy_benchmark_test`, to execute them locally and in CI environments\n129: respectively. `envoy_benchmark_test` rules call the benchmark binary from a\n130: [script](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/bazel/test_for_benchmark_wrapper.sh)\n131: which runs the benchmark with a minimal number of iterations and skipping\n132: expensive benchmarks to quickly verify that the binary is able to run to\n133: completion. In order to collect meaningful bechmarks, `bazel run -c opt` the\n134: benchmark binary target on a quiescent machine.\n135: \n136: If you would like to detect when your benchmark test is running under the\n137: wrapper, call\n138: [`Envoy::benchmark::skipExpensiveBechmarks()`](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/test/benchmark/main.h).\n139: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/envoy--v1.32.1@b35dd17bea856e19fc4e65fb05e68170841d3726/-/blob/test/README.md"}}}

At this point, you will either\\n18:   be granted maintainer status, or be given actionable feedback on any remaining gaps between the contributions\\n19:   demonstrated and those expected of maintainers, at which point you can close those gaps and reach back out.\\n20: \\n21: ## Maintainer responsibilities\\n22: \\n23: * Monitor email aliases.\\n24: * Monitor Slack (delayed response is perfectly acceptable).\\n25: * Triage GitHub issues and perform pull request reviews for other maintainers and the community.\\n26:   The areas of specialization listed in [OWNERS.md](OWNERS.md) can be used to help with routing\\n27:   an issue/question to the right person.\\n28: * Triage build and CI issues. Monitor #envoy-ci and file issues for flaking or failing builds,\\n29:   or new bugs, and either fix or find someone to fix any main build breakages.\\n30: * During GitHub issue triage, apply all applicable [labels](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/labels)\\n31:   to each new issue. Labels are extremely useful for future issue follow up. Which labels to apply\\n32:   is somewhat subjective so just use your best judgment. A few of the most important labels that are\\n33:   not self explanatory are:\\n34:   * **beginner**: Mark any issue that can reasonably be accomplished by a new contributor with\\n35:     this label.\\n36:   * **help wanted**: Unless it is immediately obvious that someone is going to work on an issue (and\\n37:     if so assign it), mark it help wanted.\\n38:   * **question**: If it's unclear if an issue is immediately actionable, mark it with the\\n39:     question label. Questions are easy to search for and close out at a later time. Questions\\n40:     can be promoted to other issue types once it's clear they are actionable (at which point the\\n41:     question label should be removed).\\n42: * Make sure that ongoing PRs are moving forward at the right pace or closing them.\\n43: * Participate when called upon in the [security release process](SECURITY.md). In extreme cases this can also occur by a vote of\n63: the maintainers per the voting process below.\n64: \n65: # xDS API shepherds\n66: \n67: The [xDS API shepherds](https://github.com/orgs/envoyproxy/teams/api-shepherds) are responsible for\n68: approving any PR that modifies the [api/](api/) tree. They ensure that API [style](api/STYLE.md) and\n69: [versioning](api/API_VERSIONING.md) policies are enforced and that a consistent approach is taken\n70: towards API evolution.\n71: \n72: The xDS API shepherds are also the xDS API maintainers; they work collaboratively with the community\n73: to drive the xDS API roadmap and review major proposed design changes. The API shepherds are\n74: intended to be representative of xDS client and control plane developers who are actively working on\n75: xDS development and evolution.\n76: \n77: As with maintainers, an API shepherd should be spending at least 25% of their time working on xDS\n78: developments and expect to be active in this space in the near future. API shepherds are expected to\n79: take on API shepherd review load and participate in meetings. They should be active on Slack `#xds`\n80: and responsive to GitHub issues and PRs on which they are tagged.\n81: \n82: The API shepherds are distinct to the [xDS working\n83: group](https://github.com/cncf/xds/blob/main/README.md), which aims to evolve xDS directionally\n84: towards a universal dataplane API. API shepherds are responsible for the execution of the xDS\n85: day-to-day and guiding xDS implementation changes. Proposals from xDS-WG will be aligned with the\n86: xDS API shepherds to ensure that xDS is heading towards the xDS goal of client and server neutral\n87: xDS. xDS API shepherds operate under the [envoyproxy](https://github.com/envoyproxy) organization\n88: but are expected to keep in mind the needs of all xDS clients (currently Envoy and gRPC, but we are\n89: aware of other in-house implementations) and the goals of xDS-WG.\n90: \n91: If you wish to become an API shepherd and satisfy the above criteria, please contact an existing\n92: API shepherd. We will factor in PR and review history to determine if the above API shepherd\n93: requirements are met. We may ask you to shadow an existing API shepherd for a period of time to\n94: build confidence in consistent application of the API guidelines to PRs.\n95: \n96: # Extension addition policy\n97: \n98: Adding new [extensions](REPO_LAYOUT.md#sourceextensions-layout) has a dedicated policy. Please\n99: see [this](./EXTENSION_POLICY.md) document for more information.\n100: \n101: # External dependency policy\n102: \n103: Adding new external dependencies has a dedicated policy. Please see [this](DEPENDENCY_POLICY.md)\n104: document for more information.\n105: \n106: # Conflict resolution and voting\n107: \n108: In general, we prefer that technical issues and maintainer membership are amicably worked out\n109: between the persons involved. If a dispute cannot be decided independently, the maintainers can be\n110: called in to decide an issue. If the maintainers themselves cannot decide an issue, the issue will\n111: be resolved by voting. The voting process is a simple majority in which each senior maintainer\n112: receives two votes and each normal maintainer receives one vote.\n113: \n114: # Adding new projects to the envoyproxy GitHub organization\n115: \n116: New projects will be added to the envoyproxy organization via GitHub issue discussion in one of the\n117: existing projects in the organization. Once sufficient discussion has taken place (~3-5 business\n118: days but depending on the volume of conversation), the maintainers of *the project where the issue\n119: was opened* (since different projects in the organization may have different maintainers) will\n120: decide whether the new project should be added. See the section above on voting if the maintainers\n121: cannot easily decide.\n122: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/envoy--v1.32.1@b35dd17bea856e19fc4e65fb05e68170841d3726/-/blob/GOVERNANCE.md"}}}

Correctly covers edge cases like `commit --amend` and\n45:   `rebase`.\n46: * Automatically running DCO and format checks on all files in the diff, before\n47:   push.\n48: \n49: [filter]: https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy-filter-example\n50: \n51: ## Fixing Format Problems\n52: \n53: If the pre-push format checks detect any problems, you can either fix the\n54: affected files manually or run the provided formatting script.\n55: \n56: To run the format fix script directly:\n57: \n58: ```console\n59: bazel run //tools/code_format:check_format -- fix && bazel run //tools/code:check -- fix -s main -v warn\n60: ```\n61: \n62: To run the format fix script under Docker:\n63: \n64: ```console\n65: ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh format'\n66: ```\n67: \n68: To run clang-tidy under Docker, run the following (this creates a full\n69: compilation db and takes a long time):\n70: \n71: ```console\n72: ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh ci/do_ci.sh clang_tidy\n73: ```\n74: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/envoy--v1.32.1@b35dd17bea856e19fc4e65fb05e68170841d3726/-/blob/support/README.md"}}}

Thus all white spaces, etc.\\n4:   issues are taken care of automatically. The Azure Pipelines will automatically check\\n5:   the code format and fail. There are make targets that can both check the format\\n6:   (check_format) as well as fix the code format for you (fix_format). Errors in\\n7:   .clang-tidy are enforced while other warnings are suggestions. Note that code and\\n8:   comment blocks designated `clang-format off` must be closed with `clang-format on`.\\n9:   To run these checks locally, see [Support Tools](support/README.md).\\n10: * Beyond code formatting, for the most part Envoy uses the\\n11:   [Google C++ style guidelines](https://google.github.io/styleguide/cppguide.html).\\n12:   The following section covers the major areas where we deviate from the Google\\n13:   guidelines.\\n14: \\n15: # Repository file layout\\n16: \\n17: * Please see [REPO_LAYOUT.md](REPO_LAYOUT.md).\\n18: \\n19: # Documentation\\n20: \\n21: * If you are modifying the data plane structurally, please keep the [Life of a\\n22:   Request](https://www.envoyproxy.io/docs/envoy/latest/intro/life_of_a_request) documentation up-to-date.\\n23: \\n24: # Deviations from Google C++ style guidelines\\n25: \\n26: * Exceptions are allowed on the control plane, though now discouraged in new code. Adding exceptions is disallowed on the data plane.\\n27: * References are always preferred over pointers when the reference cannot be null. This\\n28:   includes both const and non-const references.\\n29: * Function names should all use camel case starting with a lower case letter (e.g., `doFoo()`).\\n30: * Struct/Class member variables have a `_` postfix (e.g., `int foo_;`).\\n31: * Enum values using PascalCase (e.g., `RoundRobin`).\\n32: * 100 columns is the line limit.\\n33: * Use your GitHub name in TODO comments, e.g. `TODO(foobar): blah`.\\n34: * Smart pointers are type aliased:\\n35:   * `using FooPtr = std::unique_ptr<Foo>;`\\n36:   * `using BarSharedPtr = std::shared_ptr<Bar>;`\\n37:   * `using BlahConstSharedPtr = std::shared_ptr<const Blah>;`\\n38:   * Regular pointers (e.g. `int* foo`) should not be type aliased.\\n39: * `absl::optional<std::reference_wrapper<T>>` has a helper class in `envoy/common/optref.h`, and is type aliased:\\n40:   * `using FooOptRef = OptRef<T>;`\\n41:   * `using FooOptConstRef = OptRef<const T>;`\\n42: * If move semantics are intended, prefer specifying function arguments with `&&`.\\n43:   E.g., `void onHeaders(Http::HeaderMapPtr&& headers, ...)`. The rationale for this is that it\\n44:   forces the caller to specify `std::move(...)` or pass a temporary and makes the intention at\\n45:   the callsite clear. Otherwise, it's difficult to tell if a const reference is actually being\\n46:   passed to the called function. This is true even for `std::unique_ptr`.\\n47: * Prefer `unique_ptr` over `shared_ptr` wherever possible. `unique_ptr` makes ownership in\\n48:   production code easier to reason about. Note that this creates some test oddities where\\n49:   production code requires a `unique_ptr` but the test must still have access to the memory\\n50:   the production code is using (mock or otherwise). In these cases it is acceptable to allocate\\n51:   raw memory in a test and return it to the production code with the expectation that the\\n52:   production code will hold it in a `unique_ptr` and free it. Envoy uses the factory pattern\\n53:   quite a bit for these cases. (Search the code for \\\"factory\\\").\\n54: * Prefer explicitly sized integer types, such as uint64_t rather than size_t. In particular, use\\n55:   explicitly sized integers for data that is written to disk or involved in math that might overflow.\\n56: * The Google C++ style guide points out that [non-PoD static and global variables are forbidden](https://google.github.io/styleguide/cppguide.html#Static_and_Global_Variables).\\n57:   This _includes_ types such as `std::string`. We encourage the use of the\\n58:   advice in the [C++ FAQ on the static initialization\\n59:   fiasco](https://isocpp.org/wiki/faq/ctors#static-init-order-on-first-use) for\\n60:   how to best handle this.\\n61: * The Google C++ style guide points out that [constant vars should be named `kConstantVar`](https://google.github.io/styleguide/cppguide.html#Constant_Names).\\n62:   In the Envoy codebase we use `ConstantVar` or `CONSTANT_VAR`. If you pick `CONSTANT_VAR`,\\n63:   please be certain the name is globally significant to avoid potential conflicts with #defines,\\n64:   which are not namespace-scoped, and may appear in externally controlled header files.\\n65: * API-level comments should follow normal Doxygen conventions. Use `@param` to describe\\n66:   parameters and `@return <return-type>` for return values. Internal comments for\\n67:   methods and member variables may be regular C++ `//` comments or Doxygen at\\n68:   developer discretion. Where possible, methods should have meaningful\\n69:   documentation on expected input and state preconditions.\\n70: * Header guards should use `#pragma once`.\\n71: * All code should be inside a top-level Envoy namespace. There are some\\n72:   exceptions such as `main()` functions. When code cannot be placed inside the\\n73:   Envoy namespace there should be a comment of the form `// NOLINT(namespace-envoy)` at\\n74:   the top of the file.\\n75: * If a method that must be defined outside the `test` directory is intended to be called only\\n76:   from test code then it should have a name that ends in `ForTest()` such as `aMethodForTest()`.\\n77:   In most cases tests can and should be structured so this is not necessary.\\n78: * Tests default to StrictMock so will fail if hitting unexpected warnings. Feel free to use\\n79:   NiceMock for mocks whose behavior is not the focus of a test.\\n80: * [Thread\\n81:   annotations](https://github.com/abseil/abseil-cpp/blob/master/absl/base/thread_annotations.h),\\n82:   such as `ABSL_GUARDED_BY`, should be used for shared state guarded by\\n83:   locks/mutexes.\\n84: * Functions intended to be local to a cc file should be declared in an anonymous namespace,\\n85:   rather than using the 'static' keyword. Note that the\\n86:   [Google C++ style guide](https://google.github.io/styleguide/cppguide.html#Unnamed_Namespaces_and_Static_Variables)\\n87:    allows either, but in Envoy we prefer anonymous namespaces.\\n88: * Braces are required for all control statements include single line if, while, etc. statements.\\n89: * Don't use [mangled Protobuf enum\\n90:   names](https://developers.google.com/protocol-buffers/docs/reference/cpp-generated#enum).\\n91: \\n92: # Error handling\\n93: \\n94: A few general notes on our error handling philosophy:\\n95: \\n96: * All error code returns should be checked.\\n97: * At a very high level, our philosophy is that errors should be handled gracefully when caused by:\\n98:   - Untrusted network traffic (from downstream, upstream, or extensions like filters)\\n99:   - Raised by the Envoy process environment and are *likely* to happen\\n100:   - Third party dependency return codes\\n101: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/envoy--v1.32.1@b35dd17bea856e19fc4e65fb05e68170841d3726/-/blob/STYLE.md%3FL1-100\"}"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"5157fe49-4634-41ea-9ff4-b2bcc3cbdc75","uuid":"f187b2fd-bb38-4969-94f1-74ce852d9aec","tool_use_result":{"content":"{\"content\":\"1: # C++ coding style\\n2: \\n3: * The Envoy source code is formatted using clang-format. Where possible, methods should have meaningful\n69:   documentation on expected input and state preconditions.\n70: * Header guards should use `#pragma once`.\n71: * All code should be inside a top-level Envoy namespace. There are some\n72:   exceptions such as `main()` functions. When code cannot be placed inside the\n73:   Envoy namespace there should be a comment of the form `// NOLINT(namespace-envoy)` at\n74:   the top of the file.\n75: * If a method that must be defined outside the `test` directory is intended to be called only\n76:   from test code then it should have a name that ends in `ForTest()` such as `aMethodForTest()`.\n77:   In most cases tests can and should be structured so this is not necessary.\n78: * Tests default to StrictMock so will fail if hitting unexpected warnings. Feel free to use\n79:   NiceMock for mocks whose behavior is not the focus of a test.\n80: * [Thread\n81:   annotations](https://github.com/abseil/abseil-cpp/blob/master/absl/base/thread_annotations.h),\n82:   such as `ABSL_GUARDED_BY`, should be used for shared state guarded by\n83:   locks/mutexes.\n84: * Functions intended to be local to a cc file should be declared in an anonymous namespace,\n85:   rather than using the 'static' keyword. Note that the\n86:   [Google C++ style guide](https://google.github.io/styleguide/cppguide.html#Unnamed_Namespaces_and_Static_Variables)\n87:    allows either, but in Envoy we prefer anonymous namespaces.\n88: * Braces are required for all control statements include single line if, while, etc. statements.\n89: * Don't use [mangled Protobuf enum\n90:   names](https://developers.google.com/protocol-buffers/docs/reference/cpp-generated#enum).\n91: \n92: # Error handling\n93: \n94: A few general notes on our error handling philosophy:\n95: \n96: * All error code returns should be checked.\n97: * At a very high level, our philosophy is that errors should be handled gracefully when caused by:\n98:   - Untrusted network traffic (from downstream, upstream, or extensions like filters)\n99:   - Raised by the Envoy process environment and are *likely* to happen\n100:   - Third party dependency return codes\n101: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/envoy--v1.32.1@b35dd17bea856e19fc4e65fb05e68170841d3726/-/blob/STYLE.md%3FL1-100"}}}
